                   ; 0000 - JMP C900/JMP DEA3
                   ; 0003 - JMP CF87
                   ; 
                   ; 009c - JMP 0000 (?)
                   ; 00ae - JSR 0000 (?)
                   ; 
                   ; 00bb - jsr 0060 (?)
                   ; 
                   ; 00bf - search for first non space char (and return chr - $D0 ???)
                   ;        source: de86??
                   ;  -inc C6
                   ;   bne +
                   ;   inc c7
                   ;  +lda 0017  this operand is C6/C7
                   ;   cmp #3a   ':'
                   ;   bcs +
                   ;   cmp #20   ' '
                   ;   beq -
                   ;   sec
                   ;   sbc #d0
                   ;  +rts
                   ; 
                   ; 
                   ; 
                                   .addrs  $c000
c000: 4c a3 de     LC000           jmp     BASIC_MAIN_INIT   ;BASIC ROM Start - Init ZP

c003: 4c 7f c2     LC003           jmp     LC27F             ;To BASIC without INIT (BW monitor command)

c006: fe ce                        .dd2    $cefe
c008: d1 d0                        .dd2    $d0d1

                   ; block of BASIC commands. The address is pushed to stack and an
                   ; RTS jumps to the proper address. Hence the proper jump address is
                   ; COMMAND ADDRESS = STORED ADDR + 1

                   ; This routine can be found on the ZP starting at 00bf.
                   ; Starting from 00bf the routine increments (c6) pointer. 
                   ; At 00c5 the routine loads in the byte pointed by (c6)
                   ; (self modifying code rulez!!) and finds the first non-space
                   ; character (probably in the input buffer).
                   ; Returns if it either reached ':' or any non-space character.
                   ; At the end it sets C if the first non space char is printable (>= #$20)
                   ; 
de86: e6 c6        LDE86           inc     $c6               ;Increment BASIC console input buffer pointer?
de88: d0 02                        bne     LDE8C
de8a: e6 c7                        inc     $c7
de8c: ad           LDE8C           lda ▼   LEA60             ;Self modifying code. This LDA's operands are at $C6 and $C7
de8d: 60                           rts

de8e: ea                           .dd1    $ea
de8f: c9 3a                        cmp     #‘:’
de91: b0 0a                        bcs     LDE9D
de93: c9 20                        cmp     #‘ ’
de95: f0 ef                        beq     LDE86
de97: 38                           sec
de98: e9 30                        sbc     #$30
de9a: 38                           sec
de9b: e9 d0                        sbc     #$d0              ;C is set if the original character is ... >= #$20
de9d: 60           LDE9D           rts

de9e: 80                           .dd1    $80
de9f: 4f                           .dd1    $4f
dea0: c7                           .dd1    $c7
dea1: 52                           .dd1    $52
dea2: 58                           .dd1    $58

                   ; This is a very complicated setup routine of ZP located JMP and JSR
                   ; routines. It checks the presense of a ROM at B000 (by XOR'ing each 3rd
                   ; bytes from B000 - B042) and if the result is 4C then it's ok - does
                   ; something... Initializes stack pointer and probably system variables, 
                   ; prints out the EAGLE BASIC start text, counts the available bytes 
                   ; and prinst the BYTES FREE text also. Then starts the inline interpreter.
                   ; Probably.
                   ; 00 - JMP DEA3
                   ; 03 - JMP CF87
                   ; 10 - 00
                   ; 11 - 0D
                   ; 12 - JSR xx1E
                   ; 5e - 61
                   ; 60 - 00
                   ; 82 - FF
                   ; 9b - 03
                   ; 9c - JMP
                   ; B0 - 00
                   ; BB - JMP xx40/xx60
dea3: a2 ff        BASIC_MAIN_INIT ldx     #$ff              ;Setup ZP JMP addresses
dea5: 86 82                        stx     $82
dea7: a2 fe                        ldx     #$fe              ;why not dex ??
dea9: 9a                           txs                       ;Set SP to $FE ?
deaa: a9 a3                        lda     #$a3
deac: a0 de                        ldy     #$de
deae: 85 01                        sta     $01
deb0: 84 02                        sty     $02
deb2: a9 4c                        lda     #$4c
deb4: 85 00                        sta     $00               ;$0000   JMP $DEA3
deb6: 85 9c                        sta     $9c
deb8: 85 bb                        sta     $bb
deba: 85 03                        sta     $03               ;0003, 009c, 00bb  JMP
debc: 20 43 df                     jsr     CHECK_ROM_B000
debf: ea                           nop                       ;$00BC is either $60 or $40 (depending on DOS ROM existence)
dec0: a9 87                        lda     #$87
dec2: a0 cf                        ldy     #$cf
dec4: 85 04                        sta     $04
dec6: 84 05                        sty     $05               ;$0003   JMP $CF87
dec8: a9 20                        lda     #$20
deca: 85 12                        sta     $12
decc: a9 1e                        lda     #$1e
dece: 85 13                        sta     $13               ;$0012    JSR $xx1E
ded0: a2 1c                        ldx     #$1c
ded2: bd 85 de     LDED2           lda     LDE85,x           ;Copy DE86-DEA1 to $00BF-$00D6

                   ; Saves the Header of a program file, starting from 0280 to 037F
                   ; The sync signal length is stored in 024F
                   ; Start of the header is in 024d (shall be 0)
                   ; 280-283 - 1B
                   ; 284     - 42 ('B') - Basic ; 4F ('O') - Object
                   ; 285-28E - 10 bytes for program name
                   ; 28F     - 00
                   ; 290-291 - Start address of the block
                   ; 292-293 - Length of the block
                   ; At 0280 start the input buffer of the monitor program, be sure you fill
                   ; the header structure properly
f3e4: ad 4f 02     SAVE_HDR        lda     $024f             ;Size of the leading sync signal
f3e7: a2 00                        ldx     #$00              ;... times 256 (X)
f3e9: a0 14        LF3E9           ldy     #$14
f3eb: 20 b7 e7                     jsr     LDELAY_Y_20us     ;let's wait about 20*11us + 11us = 231us
f3ee: 8d 00 88                     sta     $8800             ;Creating the sync at the beginning of the header
f3f1: ca                           dex
f3f2: d0 f5                        bne     LF3E9
f3f4: a8                           tay                       ;Decrement A by 1
f3f5: 88                           dey
f3f6: 98                           tya
f3f7: d0 f0                        bne     LF3E9             ;loop until A == 0
f3f9: a0 08                        ldy     #$08              ;Delay 8*11 + 11 + 12 = ~0.1ms
f3fb: 20 dc ed                     jsr     LEDDC             ;Write ? bytes + 1 bit to tape, x is #ff (instead of #07)
f3fe: ea           LF3FE           nop                       ;3xNOP = 3us
f3ff: ea                           nop
f400: ea                           nop
f401: 20 d7 ed                     jsr     LEDD7             ;RTS = 6us
f404: ae 4d 02                     ldx     $024d
f407: bd 80 02                     lda     $0280,x
f40a: a2 07                        ldx     #$07
f40c: a0 06                        ldy     #$06
f40e: 20 dc ed                     jsr     LEDDC             ;Write one byte to TAPE, with custom timing
f411: ee 4d 02                     inc     $024d
f414: d0 e8                        bne     LF3FE
f416: 60                           rts
